Preface Music Theory for the stCentury Classroom openlylicensed online foursemester college music theory textbook. This text differs from other - sic theory textbooks focusing less fourpart (SATB) voiceleading and more relating harmony the phrase. Also, traditional music theory textbooks, there little emphasis motivic analysis and analysis melodic units smaller than the phrase. opinion, this led students having dif- ficulty with creating melodies, since the training they are given typically writeamelody inquarternotesinthesopranovoiceofpartwritingexercises. When the assignments those texts ask students more than this, the majority the students struggle create melody with continuity and with appropriate placement harmonies within phrase because the text had not prepared them . InMusicTheoryforthe stCenturyClassroom,studentslearnaboutmo- tive, fragment, phrase, and subphrase, well types melodic alteration like inversion, intervallic change, augmentation, diminution, rhythmic change, ornamentation, extension, and retrograde. understanding motive and sub- phrase(alsoknownasphrasesegment phrasemember),Ibelievestudents will better understand the logic and construction melodies, which will aid them creating their own music. Roman Numeral Chord Symbols Music full patterns that are similar from one piece the next. saw with minor scales, were able use scale degree numbers show the different patterns for harmonic, melodic, and natural minor, despite the fact that there are minor key signatures. Using numbers instead note names helps see these patterns. Thinking music terms numbers also helpful with transposition, which means moving melodies and/ chord progressions from one key another. Thinking music terms numbers alsohelpsustoanalyzeitandtospotsimilarpatternsbetweenmanydifferent pieces different keys. will use Roman numerals represent chords within specified key. The Roman numeral represents triad built , the st note the scale. UppercaseRomannumeralsrepresentmajortriadsandlowercaseRoman numerals ( . ., ) represent minor triads. Uppercase Roman numerals with are augmented ( . ., ), and lowercase Roman numerals with arediminished( . ., vii). (ThereisalsotheNashvilleNumberSystem, which uses Arabic numbers for chords instead Roman numerals.) Harmonic Function Nowwewilladdressnoncircle fifthsprogressions. Noticethatwehavenot included the vii chord any the shorter circle fifths progressions above. However, common axiom that Rock Roll made three chords: / , , Gan d . This because each those chords represents harmonic function. Harmonic function refers the tendency certain chords progress other chords, remain rest. Many texts music theory enumerate three harmonic functions. this text, will discuss four. . Tonic function (abbreviated ton.): The chord has tonic function, which state stability and rest. Tonic chords not demand pro- gression other chords. . Dominant function (abbreviated dom.): The and vii (chords con- tainingtheleadingtone andsupertonic )tendtoprogresstotonic( ). . . HARMONICPROGRESSIONANDHARMONICFUNCTION Chapter NonChord Tones . Introduction NonChord Tones Nonchord tones are notes that not belong the chord. Sometimes referredtoasembellishingtones andnonharmonictones, nonchordtones are classified how they are approached and left (either same tone, step, leap). There are nine types nonchord tones. NonChord Tone Approached Left Passing Tone step step same direction Neighbor Tone step step opposite direction Appoggiatura leap step Escape Tone step leap opposite direction Double Neighbor see text see text Anticipation step same note Pedal Point same note same note Suspension same note step down Retardation same note step Table . . The following qualifiers can applied nonchord tones: Accentedoccuring the beat Unaccentedoccuring the weak part the beat ( the offbeat) Chromaticnot belonging the key Metricalequal the duration the beat Submetricalsmaller than the beat Supermetricallarger than the beat . Passing Tones Passing tones are notes that pass between chord tones. CHAPTER . Chapter Form Popular Music The overall form piece popular music usually can broken down into smaller , , ,or barsections. Thematerialinthischapterisinformed John Covach essay Form Rock Music from Engaging Music: Essays Music Analysis ( . . Stein). . VerseChorus Form The VerseChorus form arguably the most common musical form present day popular music and probably familiar most readers this text. VerseChorus form, the chorus contains the hook, the memorable refrain, while the verse typically contains less memorable melodic material. clear example can found the song Are the World. : : Introduction, bars : : Verse , bars : : Verse , bars : : Chorus, bars : : Verse , bars : : Chorus, bars : : Bridge, bars : : Chorus, bars : : Chorus, bars ending with key change : end Chorus, times major with fade out Table . . : Jackson and Richie, Are The World : AjkUyX rVw Common additions the VerseChorus form, beside the bridge, are the prechorus and postchorus. CHAPTER . FORM POPULAR MUSIC : : Introduction, bars : : Verse , bars : : Prechorus, bars : : Chorus, bars : : Postchorus, bars : : Interlude, bars : : Verse , bars : : Prechorus, bars : : Chorus, bars : : Postchorus, bars : : Guitar solo, bars : : Interlude, bars : : Verse , bars : : Prechorus, bars : : Chorus, bars Table . . : Cobain, Novoselic, and Grohl, Smells Like Teen Spirit : hTWKbfoikeg worth noting that there may disagreement about labeling sections form. One person may call section prechorus, another may call first chorus, while another may call verse part . There ambiguity naming sections and disagreement expected. Therearesimple andcontrasting versechorusforms. Asimpleversechorus form has the same harmonic progression for the verse and chorus ( . ., All About That Bass). The chord progressions for the verse and chorus are dif- ferent contrasting versechorus form like Are the World. . AABA Form The AABA form associated with the hits the musicals the s and remainedoneofthemostpopularformsofpopularmusicuntilthe s,when Rock Roll became popular. Each section ( ) typically measures long. The sections contain the primary melody associate with the song whiletheBsectionprovidescontrastandisoftencalledthebridge middle eight. . . ABAC FORM : : Introduction, bars : : section ( ), bars : : section ( ), bars : : section, bars : : section ( ), bars : : section, bars (instrumental shout chorus) : : Introduction, bars (shout chorus continues) : : section ( ), bars : : section ( ), bars : : section, bars : : section ( ), bars : : Coda, bars Table . . : Gershwin, Got Rhythm : QjKTPsh Y common for one more the sections instrumental, and also common eliminate section the repeat the entire AABA form (AABAABA, for example). Other well known songs with AABA form include Over the Rainbow from The Wizard well many famous songs from the Great American Songbook George Gershwin (Let Call the Whole Thing Off, Someone Watch Over ), Cole Porter (Anything Goes, Love for Sale, Get Kick Out You), Irving Berlin (Blue Skies, Puttin the Ritz), and Jerome Kern (The Way You Look Tonight, Smoke Gets Your Eyes). TheAABAformcontinuedtobedominantintothe s(includingBeatles songs like Yesterday, Norwegian Wood, and Hey Jude, name few). The AABA form less common the present day but can found songs like The Cure Friday, Love ( ) and Norah Jones Don Know Why ( ). note terminology: the entire bar AABA form sometimes called refrain chorus, and some AABA songs are preceded verse. This means song like Someone Watch Over begins with verse and followed refrain (which could also called chorus). Other synony- mous terms you may encounter for verse the context AABA form are prelude and introduction. . ABAC Form Many popular songs from the s s were the bar ABAC form. Wellknown examples include White Christmas, Someday Prince Will Come, and When Fall Love. StarDust isanexampleofanABACformthatisusuallyperformedwith verse preceding the refrain. CHAPTER . Harmonically Closed and Open Sections harmonically closed section ends the tonic chord ( ). harmonically open section typically ends nontonic chord like , but could also end . AABA form, the sections are usually harmonically closed, ending ,andtheBsection(orbridge)isusuallyharmonicallyopen,endingon . Inversechorusform,sectionsthatleadsintothechorus(verse,prechorus, . . PRACTICE EXERCISES andbridge)areusuallyharmonicallyopen,whilechorusescanbeharmonically closed open. IfyoucomposeapieceinAABAorversechorusform,placingharmonically open and closed sections appropriately important the flow the music. Forexample,theverseandbridgeonWeAretheWorld areharmonically open (end ) while the chorus harmonically closed (ends the tonic chord, ). . Practice Exercises . THE DOUBLE PERIOD . The Double Period The Double Period. double period consists least phrases and comprised antecedent group and consequent group. The first two phrases double period are the antecedent group and the final two phrases are the consequent group, which ends with cadence that answers the less conclusive cadence ( question) that ended the antecedent group. The melodic scheme abab (four phrases) commonly encountered doubleperiod. Adoubleperiodwiththismelodicschemewouldbedescribedas parallel double period because both the antecedent group and consequent group begin with the same melody. CHAPTER . Chapter Accompanimental Textures this chapter will focus common accompanimental textures. This chapter does not make attempt catalog every known accompanimental texture. Instead, itismeanttoencourageyoutolistentotexturemoreclosely and increase your musical awareness. . Texture will consider texture terms vertical and horizontal elements. CHAPTER . ACCOMPANIMENTAL TEXTURES . Afterbeats and Offbeats . . Afterbeats The term afterbeats from Fundamentals Musical Composition noted composer and pedagogue Arnold Schoenberg. Afterbeats are repeated chords (usually eighth notes, sometimes quarter notes) that occur after the downbeat. sempre piano dolce . n b . ? . . ? : pfwIAozfjoI igure . . : Beethov , Piano SonataOp . , No. , # Inthenext example, # terb eatsarenotrepeatedcho rdsbutinsteadare passingtone figures harmonized thir . ? sempre piano dolce . n b . ? . . ? . . CHAPTER . ACCOMPANIMENTAL TEXTURES Chapter Creating Contrast Between Sec- tions Inthischapter,wewillexplorehowacomposerorarrangercancreatecontrast between different sections piece music. . The Elements Music Creating contrast usually involves varying one more the Elements Music, which are listed and explained below. Melody all know what melody , but don confuse melody with ostinato! Melody lives and breathes and has variety. Harmony this section, will associate harmony with key and mode (major versus minor). Rhythm What the most common rhythmic value section. Timbre The different tone colors different instruments, and the different tone colors individual instrument can produce. Texture Described the previous chapter existing the vertical plane (the number voices) and the horizontal plane (rhythmic activity the various voices). Articulation Staccato versus legato, short, clipped notes versus long, sustained connected notes. Dynamics Loud versus soft. Register High versus middle versus low. Modulation its simplest, modulation change key that happens within compo- sition. Inpopularmusic,thechangeofkeywilloftenbecalledakey change instead modulation. Those who study classical music theory typically reserve the term modulation for the slower and more subtle change key that occurs many classical pieces, although there are similarities between keychange inpopularmusicandtheclassicalmusictermdirectmodulation, which will study later this chapter. KEY RELATIONSHIPS relationships and pivot chords. . Key Relationships IntheBaroqueandClassicaleras, composerstypicallymodulatedtothedom- inant(whenstartinginamajorkey)ortotherelativemajor(whenstartingin minor key). the Romantic era, composers experimented with modulating more remote ( perhaps adventurous) key areas, described foreign the home key. Closely related keys have key signatures one degree sharper flat- ter than the starting key. For any major minor key, there are five closely related keys, including the relative major minor the home key. Home key flatter sharper # # # # # # # # # (relative keys with same key signature) Figure . . : Closely Related Keys with Major Home Key Key signatures that are not closely related are said foreign distantly related. will see that some types modulations from the Romanticera,likecommontonemodulations,exploitforeignkeyrelationships dramatic effect. . Compound Ternary compound ternary ternary form which one the sections (the the ) itself binary ternary form. Examples can found the minuet and trio well the capo aria. Inthenextsection,wewillexaminethedifferencesbetweenroundedbinary and ternary. . Distinguishing between Rounded Binary and Ternary homework and the test, you will encounter pieces that are five six phrases long that could rounded binary ternary. While other authors have their own means differentiate rounded binary from ternary, this text offers the following criteria consider: . Proportion: consider the proportion the contrasting section the other sections. the contrasting section too small stand alone, the form more likely rounded binary. . . DISTINGUISHINGBETWEENROUNDEDBINARYANDTERNARY . Nature: consider the nature the contrasting section. ( ) Ifthemelodyisbuiltfrommotivesfromthefirstsection,theformis likely rounded binary. Ternary form will have contrasting melody the contrasting section. ( ) the harmony consists mostly dominant pedal, chord alternating with chord, the form likely rounded binary. . Era: consider the era when the piece was written. piece Baroque composer( . .Bach, Handel, Scarlatti, Couperin)orClassicalcomposer (Haydn, Mozart, and Beethoven) more likely rounded binary form,whereasapiecebyaRomanticeracomposer(Schubert,Schumann, Chopin, Mendelssohn, and Brahms, among others) more likely ternary form. Note that these are generalities. Baroque and Clas- sical composers will write compositions ternary form and Romantic composers will write pieces rounded binary form. Consider the following piece Beethoven: CHAPTER . BINARY AND TERNARY FORMS Vivace moderato. The Four Structural Functions Music the Structural Functions chapter Practical Approach the Study Form Music, Peter Temko and Peter Spencer enumerate four structural functions. . Expository function . Transitional function . Developmental function . Terminative function . . Expository Function Music expressing expository function maintains stable tonal center and clear melodies, usually with welldefined phrases. The vast majority the music encountered binary and ternary form the last chapter was - positoryinnature. Additionally,theprimaryandsecondarythemesinasonata form are usually have expository function. Transitional Function Music transitional function moves from one tonal center another and oftenfeaturesacontrastingaccompanimentaltexturemorerhythmicallyactive than preceding expository material. Tonicizations may also occur within transition. Transitions are sometimes called bridges. Mozart and Haydn often ended their sonata form transitions with half cadence followed rest . . Voice Leading Voice leading, also known part writing, refers rules about melodic motions voices involved harmonic progressions. The primary concerns behind voice leading rules are independence parts, voicing chords, and economy melodic motion for the sake singable parts. SATB voiceleadingreferstofourpartchordsscoredforsoprano( ),alto ( ), tenor ( ), and bass ( ) voices. Threepart chords are often specified SAB (soprano, alto, bass) but could scored for any combination three voicetypes. SATBvoiceleadingwillalsobereferredtoaschoralestyle voice leading. Let set out definitions first. fugue contrapuntal composition whose form features sections called expositions and episodes Afugueexpositionisasectionthatcontainsatleastonefullstatement the subject the fugue. The fugue subject the primary melodic idea and stated each voice turn the first exposition. Theresponse,calledanswer insometexts,isthesubjectintervallically altered start the original key before modulating the dominant. Notice that the third note the subject the example below descends perfect fourth the fourth note. the response measure , the third note descends perfect fifth the fourth note. episode section that does not contain full statement the fugue subject, but instead develops the subject other prominent ideas through fragmentation and sequencing. Jazz Chord Voicings this section will examine two categories voicings. . The first category (spread voicings) has note chords with the root, rd,and thasthelowestnoteswithotherchordmembersvoicedabove, often the interval fourth fifth. (The root will always the lowest note, while the rd can voiced above below the th). . The second category (close voicings) has note chords with the bass note the left hand and the other four notes close position the right hand, usually with the th rd the chord the lowest note the right hand. Quartal, Quintal, and Secundal Harmony Quartal harmony refers chords stacked entirely ( mostly) fourths. Quintal harmony refers chords stacked entirely ( mostly) fifths. - cundal harmony refers chords stacked entirely ( mostly) seconds. Contrast these concepts with the tertian (stacked thirds) harmony encountered the majority this text. Alternative methods stacking chordsbecamemorecommonafter ascomposerssoughtwaystoinnovate and break with the past. Chapter Set Theory . Set Theory Settheoryistheanalyticaltechniquewewillusetoanalyzeexpressionistmu- sic. TheprimarycomposersassociatedwithexpressionismareArnoldSchoen- berg ( ), Anton Webern ( ), and Alban Berg ( ). this text, will associate atonal musicmusic that avoids traditional harmoniesandscaleswithexpressionism. Insteadofscalesandchords,inter- valsarethebuildingblocksofExpressionistmusic. Althoughcomposersbegan writing atonal music , there was widelyaccepted systematic ana- lytical approach that could show relationships between different pieces until Allen Forte published his seminal The Structure Atonal Music , which Forte applied set theory mathematics music. However, our approach normal form and prime form will follow the slightlymodified approach set out John Rahn his Basic Atonal Theory ( ), which the approach followed Joseph Straus his wellknown and widelyused Introduction PostTonal Theory. . . Notice that the names use for intervals carry tonal implications. augmented th would functiondifferentlythanaminor th,butinatonalmusic, theseintervalshave the same sound, are separated the same number half steps, and have tonal implications (they don have resolve any particular way). Calculating interval vector rather straightforward. First, after determing normal form, measure from ? the first note all the other notes. Second, measure from the second note # alblhigher notes (not back down the first note). Continue measuring from each successive note the notes following and you will have completed the interval vector. Before demonstrating this, important discuss the term interval class. interval class (abbreviated ) the shortest distance between two notes measured semitones. the example below, major th. However, the shortest distance between and (measure downward) minor rd. Therefore, the largest interval class (the tritone), because anyperfect th(forexample, fromCtoG)hasanintervalclassof (aperfect th) because down perfect th. . .FbORT b Major th Minor rd Perfect th Perfect th ( tw e ) ( ) Major th Minor rd Perfect th Perfect th Withthisinmind,letscompleteanintervalvectoroftheahalfdiminished thchordonG.First,arrangethenotesinasc ( , measurefrom (shortest distance first note the second, third,and fourth . and ) between and ) ic o ( Perfect th ( istance ic between and ) between and ) b b ic ic Interval Class: Mma joirc th Minor rd Perfect th Perfect th Occurrences (sho rtes t dis tance (shortest distance icb Second, measurefromthe sebcond note tobtehtewteheinr aanndd fAou)rth notes. between and ) add one tally each for interval class ( ) and . b b ic ic ic ic ic ic bb bb b b nterval Class: ic Occurrences ic ic Finally, measure from the third note the fourth note, and the interval vector will complete. add one tally for ic ;the complete interval vector bb is ,whichtellsusahalfdbbiminishedchordhaszerohalfsteps,onemajor nd (shown this voicing minor th), two minor rds, major rds, perfect th (show this voicing perfect th), and one tritone. ic b b Interval Class: Occurrences interval vector always contains digits. When interval class does not occur (the way the minor second did not occur the halfdiminished seventh chord), place zero the column for that interval class. . SET THEORY Chapter Serialism SerialismisatermthatencompassesthetwelvetonetechniqueofSchoenberg, Webern, and Berg, who were the major figures associated with expres- sionism and atonality the previous chapter set theory. will begin discussing classic twelvetone serialism before discussing nontwelvetone serialism. . TwelveTone Technique images/video- .jpg YouTube: https:// .youtube.com/watch? bQHRZ XVvI Figure . . : Arnold Schoenberg, Suite for Piano, . twelvetone composition, every note can accounted for being memberoftheoriginalseriesoroneofitspermutations,providingunitytothe piece whole. Additionally, twelvetone series repository intervals and can seen outgrowth atonal music with its emphasis interval over chord scale. The basic premises twelvetone music are follows: . All twelve notes the chromatic scale must occur . note can repeated the series until the other notes the chromatic scale have occurred (exceptions include direct repetition note, trills, and tremolos) . The series can inverted, retrograded, and the inversion can retro- graded . The order notes series remains fixed, without reordering. CHAPTER . SERIALISM . . Row Forms twelvetone series also commonly called twelvetone row, and will use the term row throughout this chapter. The four types row forms used twelvetone technique are prime ( ), retrograde ( ), inversion ( ), and retrograde inversion ( ). The prime the original row. The retrograde the prime form backward. The inversion the original row with all intervals the row inverted (going the opposite direct io ( ) . ) , ( ) sion d ( a h s # g # # d # # # o # r - backward form inverted instead the inverted form backward). Chapter Minimalism Theriseofminimalisminthe swasasignificantdevelopmentinartmusic. While four artists are typically associated with minimalism Monte Young ( . ), Terry Riley ( . ), Phillip Glass ( . ), Steve Reich ( . )wewillfocusonjusttwotechniquesinthischapter. Thefirst,additive minimalism, associated with the early minimalist pieces Philip Glass. The second, phase shifting, associated with Steve Reich. . Additive Minimalism Philip Glass version additive minimalism found the beginning his composition Two Pages ( ), adds repetition pattern but subtracts the final note the repetition. Each addition the pattern another repetition with the final note the previous repetition subtracted, can seen the example below. Phase Shifting Minimalist composer Steve Reich conceived phase shifting his early work intapemusic,notingthattapeloopsofslightlydifferinglengthscontainingthe same idea went slowly out phase and very gradually back into phase when they were repeated incessantly (see Gonna Rain from and Come Out from ). Reich applied this phaseshifting process live performance Piano Phase ( ), Violin Phase ( ), and Clapping Music ( ). Pattern: . . b . . . . b . . ( minus final note) Pattern: . . b . .
